## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration (dv/dt) in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration arises from combinations of nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and possible external driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Combined nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (coupled nonlinearities)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic + linear restoring with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — look for odd polynomial terms in x
- Even-power terms in x (x**2) indicate asymmetric potential wells and should appear when oscillation is not symmetric
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of x**2 and v (i.e., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type oscillators
- Trigonometric functions of t (sin/cos) indicate external periodic driving forces; their frequency is independent of natural frequency
- The sign of the cubic coefficient relative to the linear coefficient determines hardening (same sign as restoring) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated but not externally driven
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v**3) preserve time-reversal antisymmetry of dissipation, while even powers (v**2) break it
